<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<p>Motto: <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">"Praga Caput Rei publicae"</span>&#160;<span class="languageicon" style="font-size:81%;font-weight:normal;">(<a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>)</span><sup id="cite_ref-Vojtisek_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vojtisek-1">[1]</a></sup><br />
<small>"Prague, Head of the Republic"</small></p>
<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border: none; padding: 0;">
<div class="NavHead" style="font-size: 105%; background:transparent;text-align:center;line-height:1.15em;"><i><span style="font-weight:normal;">other historical mottos &#160;</span></i></div>

<li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><span lang="la" xml:lang="la">"Praga mater urbium"</span>&#160;<span class="languageicon" style="font-size:81%;font-weight:normal;">(<a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>)</span><br />
<span lang="cs" xml:lang="cs">"Praha matka měst"</span>&#160;<span class="languageicon" style="font-size:81%;font-weight:normal;">(<a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>)</span><sup id="cite_ref-Vojtisek_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vojtisek-1">[1]</a></sup><br />
<small>"Prague, Mother of Cities"</small></li>
<li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><span lang="la" xml:lang="la">"Praga Caput Regni"</span>&#160;<span class="languageicon" style="font-size:81%;font-weight:normal;">(<a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>)</span><sup id="cite_ref-Duchacek_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Duchacek-2">[2]</a></sup><br />
<small>"Prague, Head of the Kingdom"</small></li>
</ul>

<div style="text-align: right;">[<a href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q1085" class="extiw" title="d:Q1085">edit on Wikidata</a>]</div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr style="display:none">
<td colspan="2"></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Prague</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <span lang="cs" xml:lang="cs"><i>Praha</i></span>, <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Czech" title="Help:IPA/Czech">[ˈpraɦa]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Cs-Praha.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c7/Cs-Praha.ogg" class="internal" title="Cs-Praha.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i>Prag</i></span>) is the capital and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_the_Czech_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in the Czech Republic">largest city</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>. It is the <a href="/wiki/Largest_cities_of_the_European_Union_by_population_within_city_limits" class="mw-redirect" title="Largest cities of the European Union by population within city limits">14th largest city</a> in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> It is also the historical capital of <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>. Situated in the north-west of the country on the <a href="/wiki/Vltava" title="Vltava">Vltava</a> river, the city is home to about 1.4&#160;million people, while its <a href="/wiki/Larger_Urban_Zones" class="mw-redirect" title="Larger Urban Zones">larger urban zone</a> is estimated to have a population of 2.2&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-LUZ_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LUZ-7">[7]</a></sup> The city has a <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate climate</a>, with warm summers and chilly winters.</p>
<p>Prague has been a political, cultural, and economic centre of central Europe with waxing and waning fortunes during its history. Founded during the <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> and flourishing by the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Gothic_architecture" title="Czech Gothic architecture">Gothic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_Renaissance_architecture" title="Czech Renaissance architecture">Renaissance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Czech_Baroque_architecture" title="Czech Baroque architecture">Baroque</a> eras, Prague was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bohemia" title="Kingdom of Bohemia">kingdom of Bohemia</a> and the main residence of several <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperors</a>, most notably of <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles IV, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles IV</a> (r.&#160;1346–1378).<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> It was an important city to the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg Monarchy</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Hungarian Empire">Austro-Hungarian Empire</a>. The city played major roles in the <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Reformation" title="Bohemian Reformation">Bohemian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>, and in 20th-century history as the capital of <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>, during both World Wars and the post-war Communist era.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prague is home to a number of famous cultural attractions, many of which survived the violence and destruction of 20th-century Europe. Main attractions include the <a href="/wiki/Prague_Castle" title="Prague Castle">Prague Castle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bridge" title="Charles Bridge">Charles Bridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Old_Town_Square_(Prague)" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Town Square (Prague)">Old Town Square</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Prague_astronomical_clock" title="Prague astronomical clock">Prague astronomical clock</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Josefov" title="Josefov">Jewish Quarter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pet%C5%99%C3%ADn" title="Petřín">Petřín</a> hill and <a href="/wiki/Vy%C5%A1ehrad" title="Vyšehrad">Vyšehrad</a>. Since 1992, the extensive historic centre of Prague has been included in the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> list of <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>.</p>
<p>The city has more than ten major museums, along with numerous theatres, galleries, cinemas, and other historical exhibits. An extensive modern public transportation system connects the city. Also, it is home to a wide range of public and private schools, including <a href="/wiki/Charles_University_in_Prague" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles University in Prague">Charles University in Prague</a>, the oldest university in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prague is classified as a "Beta+" <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a> according to <a href="/wiki/GaWC" class="mw-redirect" title="GaWC">GaWC</a> studies.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Prague ranked sixth in the <a href="/wiki/Tripadvisor" class="mw-redirect" title="Tripadvisor">Tripadvisor</a> world list of best destinations in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-tripadvisor.com_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tripadvisor.com-12">[12]</a></sup> Its rich history makes it a popular tourist destination, and the city receives more than 6.4&#160;million international visitors annually, as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. Prague is the fifth most visited <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> city after <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bremner_2015_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bremner_2015-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Prague" title="History of Prague">History of Prague</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Prague" title="Timeline of Prague">Timeline of Prague</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Josef_Mathauser_-_Kn%C4%9B%C5%BEna_Libu%C5%A1e_v%C4%9B%C5%A1t%C3%AD_sl%C3%A1vu_Prahy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Josef_Mathauser_-_Kn%C4%9B%C5%BEna_Libu%C5%A1e_v%C4%9B%C5%A1t%C3%AD_sl%C3%A1vu_Prahy.jpg/220px-Josef_Mathauser_-_Kn%C4%9B%C5%BEna_Libu%C5%A1e_v%C4%9B%C5%A1t%C3%AD_sl%C3%A1vu_Prahy.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Josef_Mathauser_-_Kn%C4%9B%C5%BEna_Libu%C5%A1e_v%C4%9B%C5%A1t%C3%AD_sl%C3%A1vu_Prahy.jpg/330px-Josef_Mathauser_-_Kn%C4%9B%C5%BEna_Libu%C5%A1e_v%C4%9B%C5%A1t%C3%AD_sl%C3%A1vu_Prahy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Josef_Mathauser_-_Kn%C4%9B%C5%BEna_Libu%C5%A1e_v%C4%9B%C5%A1t%C3%AD_sl%C3%A1vu_Prahy.jpg/440px-Josef_Mathauser_-_Kn%C4%9B%C5%BEna_Libu%C5%A1e_v%C4%9B%C5%A1t%C3%AD_sl%C3%A1vu_Prahy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="483" data-file-height="310" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Josef_Mathauser_-_Kn%C4%9B%C5%BEna_Libu%C5%A1e_v%C4%9B%C5%A1t%C3%AD_sl%C3%A1vu_Prahy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The mythological princess <a href="/wiki/Libu%C5%A1e" title="Libuše">Libuše</a> prophesies the glory of Prague.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the thousand years of its existence, the city grew from a settlement stretching from <a href="/wiki/Prague_Castle" title="Prague Castle">Prague Castle</a> in the north to the fort of <a href="/wiki/Vy%C5%A1ehrad" title="Vyšehrad">Vyšehrad</a> in the south, becoming the capital of a modern European country, the Czech Republic, a member state of the European Union.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Praga_0003.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Praga_0003.JPG/170px-Praga_0003.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Praga_0003.JPG/255px-Praga_0003.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Praga_0003.JPG/340px-Praga_0003.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Praga_0003.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Prague_astronomical_clock" title="Prague astronomical clock">Prague astronomical clock</a> was first installed in 1410, making it the third-oldest astronomical clock in the world and the oldest one still working.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The region was settled as early as the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> age.<sup id="cite_ref-Demetz1997_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demetz1997-14">[14]</a></sup> Around the fifth and fourth century BC, the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> appeared in the area, later establishing settlements including an <a href="/wiki/Oppidum" title="Oppidum">oppidum</a> in Závist, a present-day suburb of Prague, and giving name to the region of Bohemia, "home of the Boii".<sup id="cite_ref-Demetz1997_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demetz1997-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bohemiaradio_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bohemiaradio-15">[15]</a></sup> In the last century BC, the Celts were slowly driven away by <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic tribes</a> (<a href="/wiki/Marcomanni" title="Marcomanni">Marcomanni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quadi" title="Quadi">Quadi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lombards" title="Lombards">Lombards</a> and possibly the <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a>), leading some to place the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Marcomanni" title="Marcomanni">Marcomanni</a> king <a href="/wiki/Maroboduus" title="Maroboduus">Maroboduus</a> on the southern Prague's site Závist.<sup id="cite_ref-marobudradio_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marobudradio-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ganz_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ganz-17">[17]</a></sup> Around the area where present-day Prague stands, the 2nd century map of <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemaios</a> mentioned a Germanic city called <i>Casurgis</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the late 5th century AD, during the great <a href="/wiki/Migration_Period" title="Migration Period">Migration Period</a> following the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>, the Germanic tribes living in Bohemia moved westwards and, in the 6th century, the <a href="/wiki/West_Slavs" title="West Slavs">Slavic tribes</a> settled Central Europe and the area of present-day Prague. In the following century, the <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">Czech tribes</a> built several fortified settlements in the area, most notably in Levý Hradec, Butovice and in the Šárka valley.<sup id="cite_ref-Demetz1997_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demetz1997-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The construction of what came to be known as the Prague Castle began near the end of the 9th century, with a fortified settlement already existing on the site in the year 800.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The first masonry under Prague Castle dates from the year 885 at the latest.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The other prominent Prague fort, the Přemyslid fort <a href="/wiki/Vy%C5%A1ehrad" title="Vyšehrad">Vyšehrad</a>, was founded in the 10th century, some 70 years later than Prague Castle.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Prague Castle is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/St._Vitus_Cathedral" title="St. Vitus Cathedral">cathedral</a>, which was founded in 1344, but completed in the 20th century.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CharlesBridgeMalaStranaPragueCzechRepublic.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/CharlesBridgeMalaStranaPragueCzechRepublic.jpg/220px-CharlesBridgeMalaStranaPragueCzechRepublic.jpg" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/CharlesBridgeMalaStranaPragueCzechRepublic.jpg/330px-CharlesBridgeMalaStranaPragueCzechRepublic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/CharlesBridgeMalaStranaPragueCzechRepublic.jpg/440px-CharlesBridgeMalaStranaPragueCzechRepublic.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2687" data-file-height="2248" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CharlesBridgeMalaStranaPragueCzechRepublic.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A view of one of the bridge towers of the Charles Bridge</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The legendary origins of Prague attribute its foundation to the 8th century Czech duchess and prophetess <a href="/wiki/Libu%C5%A1e" title="Libuše">Libuše</a> and her husband, <a href="/wiki/P%C5%99emysl,_the_Ploughman" class="mw-redirect" title="Přemysl, the Ploughman">Přemysl</a>, founder of the <a href="/wiki/P%C5%99emyslid_dynasty" title="Přemyslid dynasty">Přemyslid dynasty</a>. Legend says that Libuše came out on a rocky cliff high above the Vltava and prophesied: "I see a great city whose glory will touch the stars." She ordered a castle and a town called Praha to be built on the site.<sup id="cite_ref-Demetz1997_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demetz1997-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 17th century Jewish chronicler <a href="/wiki/David_Gans" title="David Gans">David Solomon Ganz</a>, citing <a href="/wiki/Cyriacus_Spangenberg" title="Cyriacus Spangenberg">Cyriacus Spangenberg</a>, claimed that the city was founded as Boihaem in c. 1306 BC by an ancient king, Boyya.<sup id="cite_ref-ganz_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ganz-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The region became the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Duke" title="Duke">dukes</a>, and later <a href="/wiki/King_of_Bohemia" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Bohemia">kings of Bohemia</a>. Under Roman Emperor <a href="/wiki/Otto_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Otto II, Holy Roman Emperor">Otto II</a> the area became a <a href="/wiki/Diocese" title="Diocese">bishopric</a> in 973. Until Prague was elevated to <a href="/wiki/Archbishopric" class="mw-redirect" title="Archbishopric">archbishopric</a> in 1344, it was under the jurisdiction of the <a href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Mainz" class="mw-redirect" title="Archbishopric of Mainz">Archbishopric of Mainz</a>.</p>
<p>Prague was an important seat for trading where merchants from all of Europe settled, including many Jews, as recalled in 965 by the <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Hispano-Jewish</a> merchant and traveller <a href="/wiki/Abraham_ben_Jacob" class="mw-redirect" title="Abraham ben Jacob">Ibrahim ibn Ya'qub</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Old_New_Synagogue" title="Old New Synagogue">Old New Synagogue</a> of 1270 still stands. Prague contained an important <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slave market</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the site of the ford in the Vltava river, King <a href="/wiki/Vladislaus_II,_Duke_of_Bohemia" title="Vladislaus II, Duke of Bohemia">Vladislaus I</a> had the first bridge built in 1170, the Judith Bridge (Juditin most), named in honour of his wife <a href="/wiki/Judith_of_Thuringia" title="Judith of Thuringia">Judith of Thuringia</a>. This bridge was destroyed by a flood in 1342. Some of the original foundation stones of that bridge remain.</p>
<p>In 1257, under King <a href="/wiki/Ottokar_II_of_Bohemia" title="Ottokar II of Bohemia">Ottokar II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A1_Strana" title="Malá Strana">Malá Strana</a> ("Lesser Quarter") was founded in Prague on the site of an older village in what would become the <a href="/wiki/Hrad%C4%8Dany" title="Hradčany">Hradčany</a> (Prague Castle) area. This was the district of the German people, who had the right to administer the law autonomously, pursuant to <a href="/wiki/Magdeburg_rights" title="Magdeburg rights">Magdeburg rights</a>. The new district was on the bank opposite of the <a href="/wiki/Old_Town_(Prague)" title="Old Town (Prague)">Staré Město</a> ("Old Town"), which had <a href="/wiki/Borough" title="Borough">borough</a> status and was bordered by a line of walls and fortifications.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_era_of_Charles_IV">The era of Charles IV</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The era of Charles IV">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CZ-Prag-hrad-koenigsp-kronjuw.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/CZ-Prag-hrad-koenigsp-kronjuw.jpg/220px-CZ-Prag-hrad-koenigsp-kronjuw.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/CZ-Prag-hrad-koenigsp-kronjuw.jpg/330px-CZ-Prag-hrad-koenigsp-kronjuw.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/CZ-Prag-hrad-koenigsp-kronjuw.jpg/440px-CZ-Prag-hrad-koenigsp-kronjuw.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1073" data-file-height="668" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CZ-Prag-hrad-koenigsp-kronjuw.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Crown_Jewels" title="Bohemian Crown Jewels">Czech Crown Jewels</a> are the fourth oldest in Europe</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Prague flourished during the 14th-century reign (1346–1378) of <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles IV, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles IV, Holy Roman Emperor</a> and the king of <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a> of the new <a href="/wiki/House_of_Luxembourg" title="House of Luxembourg">Luxembourg dynasty</a>. As King of Bohemia and Holy Roman Emperor, he transformed Prague into an imperial capital and it was at that time the third-largest city in Europe (after Rome and <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>).</p>
<p>He ordered the building of the <a href="/wiki/New_Town,_Prague" title="New Town, Prague">New Town</a> (Nové Město) adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Old_Town_(Prague)" title="Old Town (Prague)">Old Town</a> and laid out the design himself. The Charles Bridge, replacing the Judith Bridge destroyed in the flood just prior to his reign, was erected to connect the east bank districts to the Malá Strana and castle area. On 9 July 1357 at 5:31&#160;am, Charles IV personally laid the first foundation stone for the Charles Bridge. The exact time of laying the first foundation stone is known because the <a href="/wiki/Palindromic_number" title="Palindromic number">palindromic number</a> 135797531 was carved into the Old Town bridge tower having been chosen by the royal astrologists and numerologists as the best time for starting the bridge construction.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In 1347, he founded <a href="/wiki/Charles_University" title="Charles University">Charles University</a>, which remains the <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_universities_in_continuous_operation" title="List of oldest universities in continuous operation">oldest university</a> in Central Europe.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Vitus_Prague_September_2016-30b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/St_Vitus_Prague_September_2016-30b.jpg/170px-St_Vitus_Prague_September_2016-30b.jpg" width="170" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/St_Vitus_Prague_September_2016-30b.jpg/255px-St_Vitus_Prague_September_2016-30b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/St_Vitus_Prague_September_2016-30b.jpg/340px-St_Vitus_Prague_September_2016-30b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8434" data-file-height="9341" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Vitus_Prague_September_2016-30b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/St._Vitus_Cathedral" title="St. Vitus Cathedral">St. Vitus Cathedral</a> at <a href="/wiki/Prague_Castle" title="Prague Castle">Prague Castle</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>He began construction of the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> <a href="/wiki/St._Vitus_Cathedral" title="St. Vitus Cathedral">Saint Vitus Cathedral</a>, within the largest of the Prague Castle courtyards, on the site of the Romanesque rotunda there. Prague was elevated to an archbishopric in 1344, the year the cathedral was begun.</p>
<p>The city had a <a href="/wiki/Mint_(coin)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mint (coin)">mint</a> and was a centre of trade for German and Italian bankers and merchants. The social order, however, became more turbulent due to the rising power of the <a href="/wiki/Artisan" title="Artisan">craftsmen</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Guild" title="Guild">guilds</a> (themselves often torn by internal fights), and the increasing number of poor people.</p>
<p>The Hunger Wall, a substantial fortification wall south of Malá Strana and the Castle area, was built during a famine in the 1360s. The work is reputed to have been ordered by Charles IV as a means of providing employment and food to the workers and their families.</p>
<p>Charles IV died in 1378. During the reign of his son, King <a href="/wiki/Wenceslaus,_King_of_the_Romans" class="mw-redirect" title="Wenceslaus, King of the Romans">Wenceslaus IV</a> (1378–1419), a period of intense turmoil ensued. During Easter 1389, members of the Prague clergy announced that Jews had desecrated the host (Eucharistic wafer) and the clergy encouraged mobs to pillage, ransack and burn the Jewish quarter. Nearly the entire Jewish population of Prague (3,000 people) perished.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_banner_c1477.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Prague_banner_c1477.png/150px-Prague_banner_c1477.png" width="150" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Prague_banner_c1477.png/225px-Prague_banner_c1477.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Prague_banner_c1477.png/300px-Prague_banner_c1477.png 2x" data-file-width="936" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_banner_c1477.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Depiction of the "Prague Banner" (municipal flag dated to the 16th century)<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Star%C3%A9_M%C4%9Bsto_Pra%C5%BEsk%C3%A9_(znak).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Star%C3%A9_M%C4%9Bsto_Pra%C5%BEsk%C3%A9_%28znak%29.jpg/150px-Star%C3%A9_M%C4%9Bsto_Pra%C5%BEsk%C3%A9_%28znak%29.jpg" width="150" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8e/Star%C3%A9_M%C4%9Bsto_Pra%C5%BEsk%C3%A9_%28znak%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="165" data-file-height="198" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Star%C3%A9_M%C4%9Bsto_Pra%C5%BEsk%C3%A9_(znak).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Prague" title="Coat of arms of Prague">coat of arms of Prague</a> (1649).<sup id="cite_ref-Vojtisek_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vojtisek-1">[1]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jan_Hus" title="Jan Hus">Jan Hus</a>, a theologian and <a href="/wiki/Rector_(academia)" title="Rector (academia)">rector</a> at the Charles University, preached in Prague. In 1402, he began giving sermons in the <a href="/wiki/Bethlehem_Chapel" title="Bethlehem Chapel">Bethlehem Chapel</a>. Inspired by <a href="/wiki/John_Wycliffe" title="John Wycliffe">John Wycliffe</a>, these sermons focused on what were seen as radical reforms of a corrupt Church. Having become too dangerous for the political and religious establishment, Hus was summoned to the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Constance" title="Council of Constance">Council of Constance</a>, put on trial for <a href="/wiki/Heresy" title="Heresy">heresy</a>, and burned at the stake in <a href="/wiki/Constanz" class="mw-redirect" title="Constanz">Constanz</a> in 1415.</p>
<p>Four years later Prague experienced its <a href="/wiki/Defenestrations_of_Prague" title="Defenestrations of Prague">first defenestration</a>, when the people rebelled under the command of the Prague priest <a href="/wiki/Jan_%C5%BDelivsk%C3%BD" title="Jan Želivský">Jan Želivský</a>. Hus' death, coupled with Czech proto-nationalism and proto-Protestantism, had spurred the <a href="/wiki/Hussite_Wars" title="Hussite Wars">Hussite Wars</a>. Peasant rebels, led by the general <a href="/wiki/Jan_%C5%BDi%C5%BEka" title="Jan Žižka">Jan Žižka</a>, along with Hussite troops from Prague, defeated Emperor <a href="/wiki/Sigismund,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Sigismund, Holy Roman Emperor">Sigismund</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_V%C3%ADtkov_Hill" title="Battle of Vítkov Hill">Battle of Vítkov Hill</a> in 1420.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Hussite_Wars" title="Hussite Wars">Hussite Wars</a> when the City of Prague was attacked by "Crusader" and mercenary forces, the city militia fought bravely under the Prague Banner. This swallow-tailed banner is approximately 4 by 6 feet (1.2 by 1.8 metres), with a red field sprinkled with small white fleurs-de-lis, and a silver old Town Coat-of-Arms in the centre. The words "PÁN BŮH POMOC NAŠE" (The Lord is our Relief) appeared above the coat-of-arms, with a Hussite chalice centred on the top. Near the swallow-tails is a crescent shaped golden sun with rays protruding.</p>
<p>One of these banners was captured by Swedish troops in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Prague_(1648)" title="Battle of Prague (1648)">Battle of Prague (1648)</a>, when they captured the western bank of the Vltava river and were repulsed from the eastern bank, they placed it in the Royal Military Museum in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>; although this flag still exists, it is in very poor condition. They also took the <a href="/wiki/Codex_Gigas" title="Codex Gigas">Codex Gigas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Codex_Argenteus" title="Codex Argenteus">Codex Argenteus</a>. The earliest evidence indicates that a gonfalon with a municipal charge painted on it was used for Old Town as early as 1419. Since this city militia flag was in use before 1477 and during the Hussite Wars, it is the oldest still preserved municipal flag of Bohemia.</p>
<p>In the following two centuries, Prague strengthened its role as a merchant city. Many noteworthy Gothic buildings<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> were erected and Vladislav Hall of the Prague Castle was added.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Habsburg_era">Habsburg era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Habsburg era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bohemiae_Moraviae_et_Silesiae_(Merian)_102.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Bohemiae_Moraviae_et_Silesiae_%28Merian%29_102.jpg/220px-Bohemiae_Moraviae_et_Silesiae_%28Merian%29_102.jpg" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Bohemiae_Moraviae_et_Silesiae_%28Merian%29_102.jpg/330px-Bohemiae_Moraviae_et_Silesiae_%28Merian%29_102.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Bohemiae_Moraviae_et_Silesiae_%28Merian%29_102.jpg/440px-Bohemiae_Moraviae_et_Silesiae_%28Merian%29_102.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7325" data-file-height="4296" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bohemiae_Moraviae_et_Silesiae_(Merian)_102.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Prague panorama in 1650</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1526, the Bohemian estates elected <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Ferdinand I, Holy Roman Emperor">Ferdinand I</a> of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a>. The fervent Catholicism of its members was to bring them into conflict in Bohemia, and then in Prague, where Protestant ideas were gaining popularity.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> These problems were not pre-eminent under Holy Roman Emperor <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Rudolf II, Holy Roman Emperor">Rudolf II</a>, elected King of Bohemia in 1576, who chose Prague as his home. He lived in the Prague Castle, where his court welcomed not only astrologers and magicians but also scientists, musicians, and artists. Rudolf was an art lover too, and Prague became the capital of European culture. This was a prosperous period for the city: famous people living there in that age include the astronomers <a href="/wiki/Tycho_Brahe" title="Tycho Brahe">Tycho Brahe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler" title="Johannes Kepler">Johannes Kepler</a>, the painter <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Arcimboldo" title="Giuseppe Arcimboldo">Arcimboldo</a>, the alchemists <a href="/wiki/Edward_Kelley" title="Edward Kelley">Edward Kelley</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Dee" title="John Dee">John Dee</a>, the poet <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Jane_Weston" title="Elizabeth Jane Weston">Elizabeth Jane Weston</a>, and others.</p>
<p>In 1618, the famous <a href="/wiki/Defenestrations_of_Prague" title="Defenestrations of Prague">second defenestration of Prague</a> provoked the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>, a particularly harsh period for Prague and Bohemia. <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Ferdinand II, Holy Roman Emperor">Ferdinand II</a> of Habsburg was deposed, and his place as King of Bohemia taken by <a href="/wiki/Frederick_V,_Elector_Palatine" class="mw-redirect" title="Frederick V, Elector Palatine">Frederick V, Elector Palatine</a>; however his army was crushed in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_White_Mountain" title="Battle of White Mountain">Battle of White Mountain</a> (1620) not far from the city. Following this in 1621 was an execution of 27 Czech leaders (involved in the uprising) in Old Town Square and the exiling of many others. The city suffered subsequently during the war under <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxon</a> (1631) and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Prague_(1648)" title="Battle of Prague (1648)">Battle of Prague (1648)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Prague began a steady decline which reduced the population from the 60,000 it had had in the years before the war to 20,000. In the second half of the 17th century Prague's population began to grow again. <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="History of the Jews in the Czech Republic">Jews</a> have been in Prague since the end of the 10th century and, by 1708, they accounted for about a quarter of Prague's population.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frantisek_Palacky_monument.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Frantisek_Palacky_monument.jpg/170px-Frantisek_Palacky_monument.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Frantisek_Palacky_monument.jpg/255px-Frantisek_Palacky_monument.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Frantisek_Palacky_monument.jpg/340px-Frantisek_Palacky_monument.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frantisek_Palacky_monument.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Monument to <a href="/wiki/Franti%C5%A1ek_Palack%C3%BD" title="František Palacký">František Palacký</a>, a significant member of the <a href="/wiki/Czech_National_Revival" title="Czech National Revival">Czech National Revival</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1689, a great fire devastated Prague, but this spurred a renovation and a rebuilding of the city. In 1713–14, a major outbreak of <a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">plague</a> hit Prague one last time, killing 12,000 to 13,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1744 <a href="/wiki/Frederick_the_Great" title="Frederick the Great">Frederick the Great</a> of Prussia invaded Bohemia and obtained possession of Prague after a severe and prolonged bombardment, in the course of which a large part of the town was destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-33">[33]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Prague_(1757)" title="Battle of Prague (1757)">Battle of Prague</a> in 1757 <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussian</a> bombardment<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-33">[33]</a></sup> destroyed more than one quarter of the city and heavily damaged St. Vitus Cathedral. However next month after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kol%C3%ADn" title="Battle of Kolín">Battle of Kolín</a>, Frederick the Great lost and had to retreat from Bohemia.</p>
<p>The economic rise continued through the 18th century, and the city in 1771 had 80,000 inhabitants. Many of these were rich merchants and nobles who enriched the city with a host of palaces, churches and gardens full of art and <a href="/wiki/Music_from_Eighteenth-Century_Prague" title="Music from Eighteenth-Century Prague">music</a>, creating a <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> style renowned throughout the world.</p>
<p>In 1784, under <a href="/wiki/Joseph_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph II, Holy Roman Emperor">Joseph II</a>, the four municipalities of Malá Strana, Nové Město, Staré Město, and Hradčany were merged into a single entity. The Jewish district, called <a href="/wiki/Josefov" title="Josefov">Josefov</a>, was included only in 1850. The <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> had a strong effect in Prague, as factories could take advantage of the coal mines and ironworks of the nearby region. A first suburb, <a href="/wiki/Karl%C3%ADn" title="Karlín">Karlín</a>, was created in 1817, and twenty years later the population exceeded 100,000.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848" title="Revolutions of 1848">The revolutions in Europe in 1848</a> also touched Prague, but they were fiercely suppressed. In the following years the <a href="/wiki/Czech_National_Revival" title="Czech National Revival">Czech National Revival</a> began its rise, until it gained the majority in the town council in 1861. Prague had a German-speaking majority in 1848, but by 1880 the number of German speakers had decreased to 14% (42,000), and by 1910 to 6.7% (37,000), due to a massive increase of the city's overall population caused by the influx of <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">Czechs</a> from the rest of Bohemia and <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravia</a> and also due to return of social status importance of the Czech language.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Czechoslovak_Republic">First Czechoslovak Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: First Czechoslovak Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/First_Czechoslovak_Republic" title="First Czechoslovak Republic">First Czechoslovak Republic</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_liberation_1945_konev.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Prague_liberation_1945_konev.jpg/220px-Prague_liberation_1945_konev.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Prague_liberation_1945_konev.jpg/330px-Prague_liberation_1945_konev.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Prague_liberation_1945_konev.jpg/440px-Prague_liberation_1945_konev.jpg 2x" data-file-width="770" data-file-height="491" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_liberation_1945_konev.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Prague liberated by <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> in May 1945</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>World War I ended with the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Hungarian Empire">Austro-Hungarian Empire</a> and the creation of Czechoslovakia. Prague was chosen as its capital and Prague Castle as the seat of president <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1%C5%A1_Garrigue_Masaryk" title="Tomáš Garrigue Masaryk">Tomáš Masaryk</a>. At this time Prague was a true European capital with highly developed industry. By 1930, the population had risen to 850,000.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Czechoslovakia" title="German occupation of Czechoslovakia">German occupation of Czechoslovakia</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hitler" class="mw-redirect" title="Hitler">Hitler</a> ordered the <a href="/wiki/German_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="German Army (Wehrmacht)">German Army</a> to enter Prague on 15 March 1939, and from Prague Castle proclaimed <a href="/wiki/Protectorate_of_Bohemia_and_Moravia" title="Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia">Bohemia and Moravia a German protectorate</a>. For most of its history, Prague had been a multi-ethnic city with important Czech, German and (mostly native German-speaking) Jewish populations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> From 1939, when the country was occupied by <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>, and during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, most Jews were <a href="/wiki/Holocaust" class="mw-redirect" title="Holocaust">deported and killed</a> by the Germans. In 1942, Prague was witness to the assassination of one of the most powerful men in <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>&#160;– <a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Heydrich" title="Reinhard Heydrich">Reinhard Heydrich</a>&#160;– during <a href="/wiki/Operation_Anthropoid" title="Operation Anthropoid">Operation Anthropoid</a>, accomplished by Czechoslovak national heroes <a href="/wiki/Jozef_Gab%C4%8D%C3%ADk" title="Jozef Gabčík">Jozef Gabčík</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jan_Kubi%C5%A1" title="Jan Kubiš">Jan Kubiš</a>. Hitler ordered bloody reprisals.</p>
<p>At the end of the war, <a href="/wiki/1945_Bombing_of_Prague" title="1945 Bombing of Prague">Prague suffered several bombing raids</a> by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Forces" title="United States Army Air Forces">US Army Air Forces</a>. 701 people were killed, more than 1,000 people were injured and some of buildings, factories and historical landmarks (<a href="/wiki/Emmaus_Monastery" title="Emmaus Monastery">Emmaus Monastery</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Faust_House_(Prague)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Faust House (Prague) (page does not exist)">Faust House</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vinohrady_Synagogue&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Vinohrady Synagogue (page does not exist)">Vinohrady Synagogue</a>) were destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-Bombing_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bombing-34">[34]</a></sup> Many historic structures in Prague, however, escaped the destruction of the war and the damage was small compared to the total destruction of many other cities in that time. According to American pilots, it was the result of a navigational mistake.</p>
<p>On 5 May 1945, two days before Germany capitulated, an <a href="/wiki/Prague_uprising" title="Prague uprising">uprising</a> against Germany occurred. Four days later, the <a href="/wiki/3rd_Shock_Army" title="3rd Shock Army">3rd Shock Army</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> liberated the city. The majority (about 50,000 people) of the German population of Prague either fled or were <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_Germans_after_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Expulsion of Germans after World War II">expelled</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Bene%C5%A1_decrees" title="Beneš decrees">Beneš decrees</a> in the aftermath of the war.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War">Cold War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Cold War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Czechoslovakia_(1948%E2%80%9389)" title="History of Czechoslovakia (1948–89)">History of Czechoslovakia (1948–89)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Havla_1989.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Havla_1989.jpg/220px-Havla_1989.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Havla_1989.jpg/330px-Havla_1989.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Havla_1989.jpg/440px-Havla_1989.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1760" data-file-height="1176" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Havla_1989.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Velvet_Revolution" title="Velvet Revolution">Velvet Revolution</a> in November 1989</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Prague was a city in the territory of military and political control of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a>). The biggest <a href="/wiki/Stalin_Monument_(Prague)" title="Stalin Monument (Prague)">Stalin Monument</a> was unveiled on <a href="/wiki/Letn%C3%A1" title="Letná">Letná</a> hill in 1955 and destroyed in 1962. The 4th Czechoslovakian Writers' Congress held in the city in June 1967 took a strong position against the regime.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> On 31 October 1967 students demonstrated at <a href="/wiki/Strahov_(district_of_Prague)" title="Strahov (district of Prague)">Strahov</a>. This spurred the new secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist Party">Communist Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Dub%C4%8Dek" title="Alexander Dubček">Alexander Dubček</a>, to proclaim a new deal in his city's and country's life, starting the short-lived season of the "socialism with a human face". It was the <i>"<a href="/wiki/Prague_Spring" title="Prague Spring">Prague Spring</a>"</i>, which aimed at the renovation of institutions in a democratic way. The other <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> member countries, except <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania" title="Socialist Republic of Romania">Romania</a> and <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Socialist_Republic_of_Albania" title="People's Socialist Republic of Albania">Albania</a>, reacted with the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact_invasion_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia">invasion</a> of Czechoslovakia and the capital on 21 August 1968 by tanks, suppressing any attempt at reform. <a href="/wiki/Jan_Palach" title="Jan Palach">Jan Palach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jan_Zaj%C3%ADc" title="Jan Zajíc">Jan Zajíc</a> committed suicide by <a href="/wiki/Self-immolation" title="Self-immolation">self-immolation</a> in January and February 1969 to protest against the "normalization" of the country.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_Velvet_Revolution">After Velvet Revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: After Velvet Revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mrakodrapy_v_praze.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Mrakodrapy_v_praze.jpg/220px-Mrakodrapy_v_praze.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Mrakodrapy_v_praze.jpg/330px-Mrakodrapy_v_praze.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Mrakodrapy_v_praze.jpg/440px-Mrakodrapy_v_praze.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2875" data-file-height="2155" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mrakodrapy_v_praze.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Prague high-rise buildings</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1989, after the riot police beat back a peaceful student demonstration, the <a href="/wiki/Velvet_Revolution" title="Velvet Revolution">Velvet Revolution</a> crowded the streets of Prague, and the <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovak" class="mw-redirect" title="Czechoslovak">Czechoslovak</a> capital benefited greatly from the new mood. In 1993, after the split of Czechoslovakia, Prague became the capital city of the new Czech Republic. From 1995 high-rise buildings began to be built in Prague in large quantities. In the late 1990s, Prague again became an important cultural centre of Europe and was notably influenced by <a href="/wiki/Globalisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Globalisation">globalisation</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. In 2000, <a href="/wiki/IMF" class="mw-redirect" title="IMF">IMF</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> summits took place in Prague. In 2002, Prague suffered from <a href="/wiki/2002_European_floods" title="2002 European floods">widespread floods</a> that damaged buildings and its underground transport system.</p>
<p>Prague <a href="/wiki/Prague_bid_for_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Prague bid for the 2016 Summer Olympics">launched a bid</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Summer Olympics</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> but failed to make the candidate city <a href="/wiki/Shortlist" class="mw-redirect" title="Shortlist">shortlist</a>. In June 2009, as the result of financial pressures from the global recession, Prague's officials also chose to cancel the city's planned bid for the <a href="/wiki/2020_Summer_Olympics" title="2020 Summer Olympics">2020 Summer Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_European_cities_in_different_languages:_M-P#P" class="mw-redirect" title="Names of European cities in different languages: M-P">Names in different languages</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vltava_in_Prague.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Vltava_in_Prague.jpg/220px-Vltava_in_Prague.jpg" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Vltava_in_Prague.jpg/330px-Vltava_in_Prague.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Vltava_in_Prague.jpg/440px-Vltava_in_Prague.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3394" data-file-height="1995" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vltava_in_Prague.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bridges over the River Vltava, as seen from Letná</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Czech name Praha is derived from an old <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic</a> word, <i>práh</i>, which means "<a href="/wiki/Ford_(crossing)" title="Ford (crossing)">ford</a>" or "<a href="/wiki/Rapid" class="mw-redirect" title="Rapid">rapid</a>", referring to the city's origin at a crossing point of the Vltava river.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The same etymology is associated with the <a href="/wiki/Praga" title="Praga">Praga district of Warsaw</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another view to the origin of name is also related to the Czech word <i>práh</i> (in the mean of a <a href="/wiki/Threshold_(door)" title="Threshold (door)">threshold</a>) and a legendary etymology connects the name of the city with princess <a href="/wiki/Libu%C5%A1e" title="Libuše">Libuše</a>, prophetess and a wife of mythical founder of the <a href="/wiki/P%C5%99emyslid_dynasty" title="Přemyslid dynasty">Přemyslid dynasty</a>. She is said to have ordered the city <i>"to be built where a man hews a threshold of his house"</i>. The Czech <i>práh</i> might thus be understood to refer to rapids or fords in the river, the edge of which could have acted as a means of fording the river&#160;– thus providing a "threshold" to the castle.</p>
<p>Another derivation of the name <i>Praha</i> is suggested from <i>na prazě</i>, the original term for the <a href="/wiki/Shale" title="Shale">shale</a> hillside rock upon which the original castle was built. At that time, the castle was surrounded by forests, covering the nine hills of the future city&#160;– the <a href="/wiki/Old_Town,_Prague" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Town, Prague">Old Town</a> on the opposite side of the river, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Town" class="mw-redirect" title="Lesser Town">Lesser Town</a> beneath the existing castle, appeared only later.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The English spelling of the city's name is borrowed from <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>. Prague is also called the <i>"City of a Hundred <a href="/wiki/Spire" title="Spire">Spires</a>"</i>, based on a count by 19th century mathematician <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Bolzano" title="Bernard Bolzano">Bernard Bolzano</a>, today's count is estimated by Prague Information Service at 500.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Nicknames for Prague have also included: the Golden City, the Mother of Cities and the Heart of Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Prague is situated on the <a href="/wiki/Vltava" title="Vltava">Vltava</a> river, at 50°05"N and 14°27"E.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> in the centre of the Bohemian Basin. Prague is approximately at the same latitude as Frankfurt, Germany;<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Paris, France;<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> and Vancouver, Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1408px;">

</div>
</div>

</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to the 2011 census, about 14% of the city inhabitants were foreigners, the highest proportion in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>

<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_SPOT_1030.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Prague_SPOT_1030.jpg/220px-Prague_SPOT_1030.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Prague_SPOT_1030.jpg/330px-Prague_SPOT_1030.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Prague_SPOT_1030.jpg/440px-Prague_SPOT_1030.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_SPOT_1030.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Prague seen from <a href="/wiki/SPOT_(satellite)" title="SPOT (satellite)">satellite</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city of Prague lies between <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (Köppen Cfb/Dfb). The winters are relatively cold with average temperatures at about freezing point, and with very little sunshine. Snow cover can be common between mid-November and late March although snow accumulations of more than 20&#160;cm (8&#160;in) are infrequent. There are also a few periods of mild temperatures in winter. Summers usually bring plenty of sunshine and the average high temperature of 24&#160;°C (75&#160;°F). Nights can be quite cool even in summer, though. Precipitation in Prague (and most of the Bohemian lowland) is rather low (just over 500&#160;mm&#160;[20&#160;in] per year) since it is located in the <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">rain shadow</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sudetes" title="Sudetes">Sudetes</a> and other mountain ranges. The driest season is usually winter while late spring and summer can bring quite heavy rain, especially in form of thundershowers. <a href="/wiki/Inversion_(meteorology)" title="Inversion (meteorology)">Temperature inversions</a> are relatively common between mid-October and mid-March bringing foggy, cold days and sometimes moderate air pollution. Prague is also a windy city with common sustained western winds and an average wind speed of 16&#160;km/h (9.9&#160;mph) that often help break temperature inversions and clear the air in cold months.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Prague" title="List of museums in Prague">museums</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theatre_of_the_Czech_Republic#List_of_important_Czech_theatres_and_theatre_companies" title="Theatre of the Czech Republic">theatres and operas</a>,&#160;and galleries and libraries</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Praha_Veletr%C5%BEn%C3%AD_pal%C3%A1c_jih.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Praha_Veletr%C5%BEn%C3%AD_pal%C3%A1c_jih.jpg/220px-Praha_Veletr%C5%BEn%C3%AD_pal%C3%A1c_jih.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Praha_Veletr%C5%BEn%C3%AD_pal%C3%A1c_jih.jpg/330px-Praha_Veletr%C5%BEn%C3%AD_pal%C3%A1c_jih.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Praha_Veletr%C5%BEn%C3%AD_pal%C3%A1c_jih.jpg/440px-Praha_Veletr%C5%BEn%C3%AD_pal%C3%A1c_jih.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2144" data-file-height="1492" /></a>

Veletržní palác houses the largest collection of <a href="/wiki/National_Gallery_in_Prague" title="National Gallery in Prague">National Gallery</a> art</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_07-2016_View_from_Petrinska_Tower_img4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Prague_07-2016_View_from_Petrinska_Tower_img4.jpg/220px-Prague_07-2016_View_from_Petrinska_Tower_img4.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Prague_07-2016_View_from_Petrinska_Tower_img4.jpg/330px-Prague_07-2016_View_from_Petrinska_Tower_img4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Prague_07-2016_View_from_Petrinska_Tower_img4.jpg/440px-Prague_07-2016_View_from_Petrinska_Tower_img4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4847" data-file-height="3029" /></a>
