National Theatre in Prague</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Praha_Rudolfinum_isometric.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Praha_Rudolfinum_isometric.jpg/220px-Praha_Rudolfinum_isometric.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Praha_Rudolfinum_isometric.jpg/330px-Praha_Rudolfinum_isometric.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Praha_Rudolfinum_isometric.jpg/440px-Praha_Rudolfinum_isometric.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2177" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Praha_Rudolfinum_isometric.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Rudolfinum" title="Rudolfinum">Rudolfinum</a>, a concert and exhibition hall</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_Congress_Centre_(1).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Prague_Congress_Centre_%281%29.JPG/220px-Prague_Congress_Centre_%281%29.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Prague_Congress_Centre_%281%29.JPG/330px-Prague_Congress_Centre_%281%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Prague_Congress_Centre_%281%29.JPG/440px-Prague_Congress_Centre_%281%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_Congress_Centre_(1).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Prague_Congress_Centre" title="Prague Congress Centre">Prague Congress Centre</a> has hosted the <a href="/wiki/IMF" class="mw-redirect" title="IMF">IMF</a>-<a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">WBG</a> meeting and <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> summit</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city is traditionally one of the cultural centres of Europe, hosting many cultural events. Some of the significant cultural institutions include the <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre_(Prague)" title="National Theatre (Prague)">National Theatre</a> (<i>Národní Divadlo</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Estates_Theatre" title="Estates Theatre">Estates Theatre</a> (<i>Stavovské or Tylovo</i> or <i>Nosticovo divadlo</i>), where the premières of <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Mozart</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Don_Giovanni" title="Don Giovanni">Don Giovanni</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/La_clemenza_di_Tito" title="La clemenza di Tito">La clemenza di Tito</a></i> were held. Other major cultural institutions are the <a href="/wiki/Rudolfinum" title="Rudolfinum">Rudolfinum</a> which is home to the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Philharmonic" title="Czech Philharmonic">Czech Philharmonic Orchestra</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Municipal_House" title="Municipal House">Municipal House</a> which is home to the <a href="/wiki/Prague_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Prague Symphony Orchestra">Prague Symphony Orchestra</a>. The <a href="/wiki/State_Opera_(Prague)" title="State Opera (Prague)">Prague State Opera</a> (Státní opera) performs at the Smetana Theatre.</p>
<p>The city has many world-class museums, including the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_(Prague)" title="National Museum (Prague)">National Museum</a> (Národní muzeum), the Museum of the Capital City of Prague, the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Museum_in_Prague" title="Jewish Museum in Prague">Jewish Museum in Prague</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Alfons_Mucha" class="mw-redirect" title="Alfons Mucha">Alfons Mucha</a> Museum, the African-Prague Museum, the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Decorative_Arts_in_Prague" title="Museum of Decorative Arts in Prague">Museum of Decorative Arts in Prague</a>, the <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A1prstek_Museum" title="Náprstek Museum">Náprstek Museum</a> (Náprstkovo Muzeum), the <a href="/wiki/Josef_Sudek_Gallery" title="Josef Sudek Gallery">Josef Sudek Gallery</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Josef_Sudek_Studio" title="The Josef Sudek Studio">The Josef Sudek Studio</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Clementinum" title="Clementinum">National Library</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Gallery_in_Prague" title="National Gallery in Prague">National Gallery</a>, which manages the largest collection of art in the Czech Republic.</p>
<p>There are hundreds of concert halls, galleries, cinemas and music clubs in the city. It hosts <a href="/wiki/List_of_festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="List of festivals">music festivals</a> including the <a href="/wiki/Prague_Spring_International_Music_Festival" title="Prague Spring International Music Festival">Prague Spring International Music Festival</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Prague_Autumn_International_Music_Festival" title="Prague Autumn International Music Festival">Prague Autumn International Music Festival</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Prague_International_Organ_Festival" title="Prague International Organ Festival">Prague International Organ Festival</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prague_International_Jazz_Festival" title="Prague International Jazz Festival">Prague International Jazz Festival</a>. Film festivals include the <a href="/wiki/Febiofest" title="Febiofest">Febiofest</a>, the <a href="/wiki/One_World_Film_Festival" title="One World Film Festival">One World Film Festival</a> and Echoes of the <a href="/wiki/Karlovy_Vary_International_Film_Festival" title="Karlovy Vary International Film Festival">Karlovy Vary International Film Festival</a>. The city also hosts the <a href="/wiki/Prague_Writers%27_Festival" title="Prague Writers' Festival">Prague Writers' Festival</a>, the Prague Folklore Days, Prague Advent Choral Meeting the <i>Summer <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare" class="mw-redirect" title="Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a> Festival</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Prague_Fringe_Festival" title="Prague Fringe Festival">Prague Fringe Festival</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Roma_Festival" title="World Roma Festival">World Roma Festival</a>, as well as the hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Vernissage" title="Vernissage">Vernissages</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fashion_show" title="Fashion show">fashion shows</a>.</p>
<p>Many films have been made at <a href="/wiki/Barrandov_Studios" title="Barrandov Studios">Barrandov Studios</a> and at Prague Studios. Hollywood films set in Prague include <i><a href="/wiki/Mission:_Impossible" title="Mission: Impossible">Mission Impossible</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/XXx_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="XXx (film)">xXx</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Blade_II" title="Blade II">Blade II</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Alien_vs._Predator_(film)" title="Alien vs. Predator (film)">Alien vs. Predator</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doom_(film)" title="Doom (film)">Doom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chronicles_of_Narnia" class="mw-redirect" title="Chronicles of Narnia">Chronicles of Narnia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hellboy_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hellboy (film)">Hellboy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_Tails" title="Red Tails">Red Tails</a>, Children of Dune and <i><a href="/wiki/Van_Helsing" class="mw-redirect" title="Van Helsing">Van Helsing</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Prague_Studios_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prague_Studios-55">[55]</a></sup> Other Czech films shot in Prague include <i><a href="/wiki/Empties" title="Empties">Empties</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/EuroTrip" title="EuroTrip">EuroTrip</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Amadeus" title="Amadeus">Amadeus</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fifth_Horseman_is_Fear" class="mw-redirect" title="The Fifth Horseman is Fear">The Fifth Horseman is Fear</a></i>. Also, the romantic music video "<a href="/wiki/Never_Tear_Us_Apart" title="Never Tear Us Apart">Never Tear Us Apart</a>" by <a href="/wiki/INXS" title="INXS">INXS</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Diamonds_from_Sierra_Leone" title="Diamonds from Sierra Leone">Diamonds from Sierra Leone</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> was shot in the city, and features shots of the Charles Bridge and the Astronomical Clock, among other famous landmarks. <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Stop_the_Music_(Rihanna_song)" title="Don't Stop the Music (Rihanna song)">Don't Stop the Music</a>" video was filmed at Prague's Radost FX Club. The city was also the setting for the film <i><a href="/wiki/Dungeons_%26_Dragons_(film)" title="Dungeons &amp; Dragons (film)">Dungeons and Dragons</a></i> in 2000. The music video "<a href="/wiki/Silver_and_Cold" title="Silver and Cold">Silver and Cold</a>" by <a href="/wiki/AFI_(band)" title="AFI (band)">AFI</a>, an American rock band, was also filmed in Prague. Many Indian films have also been filmed in the city including <i><a href="/wiki/Yuvraaj" class="mw-redirect" title="Yuvraaj">Yuvraaj</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Drona" title="Drona">Drona</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Rockstar_(2011_film)" title="Rockstar (2011 film)">Rockstar</a></i>.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Forbes_Traveler" class="mw-redirect" title="Forbes Traveler">Forbes Traveler</a></i> magazine and <a href="/wiki/TripAdvisor" title="TripAdvisor">TripAdvisor</a> listed <a href="/wiki/Prague_Zoo" title="Prague Zoo">Prague Zoo</a> among the world's best zoos.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes-zoo_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-zoo-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the growth of low-cost airlines in Europe, Prague has become a popular weekend city destination allowing tourists to visit its many museums and cultural sites as well as try its famous Czech beers and hearty cuisine.</p>
<p>The city has many buildings by renowned architects, including <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Loos" title="Adolf Loos">Adolf Loos</a> (<a href="/wiki/Villa_M%C3%BCller" title="Villa Müller">Villa Müller</a>), <a href="/wiki/Frank_O._Gehry" class="mw-redirect" title="Frank O. Gehry">Frank O. Gehry</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dancing_House" title="Dancing House">Dancing House</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Jean_Nouvel" title="Jean Nouvel">Jean Nouvel</a> (<a href="/wiki/Golden_Angel" title="Golden Angel">Golden Angel</a>).</p>
<p>Recent major events held in Prague:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> Summit 2000</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> Summit 2002</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> Session 2004</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union" title="International Astronomical Union">IAU</a> General Assembly 2006 (<a href="/wiki/IAU_definition_of_planet" title="IAU definition of planet">Definition of planet</a>)</li>
<li>EU &amp; USA Summit 2009</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">Czech</a> <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_the_Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Presidency of the Council of the European Union">Presidency of the Council of the European Union</a> 2009</li>
<li>USA &amp; Russia Summit 2010 (signing of the <a href="/wiki/START_treaty_(2010)" class="mw-redirect" title="START treaty (2010)">New START treaty</a>)</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2008 the <a href="/wiki/Allegro_(restaurant)" title="Allegro (restaurant)">Allegro</a> restaurant received the first <a href="/wiki/Michelin_Guide" title="Michelin Guide">Michelin star</a> in the whole of the post-Communist part of Central Europe. It retained its star until 2011. As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> there are three Michelin-starred restaurants in Prague: Alcron, La Degustation Bohême Bourgeoise and Field.</p>
<p>In Malá Strana, Staré Město, <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDi%C5%BEkov" title="Žižkov">Žižkov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nusle" title="Nusle">Nusle</a> there are hundreds of restaurants, bars and pubs, especially with <a href="/wiki/Czech_beer" class="mw-redirect" title="Czech beer">Czech beer</a>. Prague also hosts the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Beer_Festival" title="Czech Beer Festival">Czech Beer Festival</a> (Český pivní festival), which is the largest <a href="/wiki/Beer_festival" title="Beer festival">beer festival</a> in the Czech Republic, held for 17 days every year in May. At the festival, more than 70 brands of Czech beer can be tasted.</p>
<p>Prague is home to many <a href="/wiki/Brewery" title="Brewery">breweries</a> including:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul>
<li>Pivovary <a href="/wiki/Staropramen_Brewery" title="Staropramen Brewery">Staropramen</a> (Praha 5)</li>
<li>První novoměstský restaurační pivovar (Praha 1)</li>
<li>Pivovar <a href="/wiki/U_Flek%C5%AF" title="U Fleků">U Fleků</a> (Praha 1)</li>
<li>Klášterní pivovar Strahov (Praha 1)</li>
<li>Pivovar Pražský most u Valšů (Praha 1)</li>
<li>Pivovarský Hotel U Medvídků (Praha 1)</li>
<li>Pivovarský dům (Praha 2)</li>
<li>Jihoměstský pivovar (Praha 4)</li>
<li>Sousedský pivovar U Bansethů (Praha 4)</li>
<li>Vyukový a výzkumný pivovar&#160;– Suchdolský Jeník (Praha 6)</li>
<li>Pivovar U Bulovky (Praha 8)</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zizkov_tv_tower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Zizkov_tv_tower.jpg/170px-Zizkov_tv_tower.jpg" width="170" height="299" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Zizkov_tv_tower.jpg/255px-Zizkov_tv_tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Zizkov_tv_tower.jpg/340px-Zizkov_tv_tower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="831" data-file-height="1463" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zizkov_tv_tower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/%C5%BDi%C5%BEkov_Television_Tower" title="Žižkov Television Tower">Žižkov Television Tower</a> with crawling "babies"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Prague's economy accounts for 25% of the Czech GDP<sup id="cite_ref-CDAP_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDAP-57">[57]</a></sup> making it the highest performing regional economy of the country. According to the <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>, as of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, its GDP per capita in <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power standard</a> is €42,800. Prague ranked the 5th best-performing European <a href="/wiki/Nomenclature_of_Territorial_Units_for_Statistics" title="Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics">NUTS</a> two-level region at 172 percent of the EU-27 average.<sup id="cite_ref-RHDP_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RHDP-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city is the site of the European headquarters of many international companies.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Prague employs almost a fifth of the entire Czech workforce, and its wages are significantly above average (~+25%). In December 2015, average salaries available in Prague reached 35,853 CZK, an annual increase of 3.4%, which was nevertheless lower than national increase of 3.9% both in nominal and real terms. (Inflation in Prague was 0.5% in December, compared with 0.1% nationally.)<sup id="cite_ref-RHDP_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RHDP-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Since 1990, the city's economic structure has shifted from industrial to service-oriented. Industry is present in sectors such as pharmaceuticals, printing, food processing, manufacture of transport equipment, computer technology and electrical engineering. In the service sector, financial and commercial services, trade, restaurants, hospitality and public administration are the most significant. <a href="/wiki/Service_(economics)" title="Service (economics)">Services</a> account for around 80 percent of employment. There are 800,000 employees in Prague, including 120,000 commuters.<sup id="cite_ref-CDAP_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDAP-57">[57]</a></sup> The number of (legally registered) foreign residents in Prague has been increasing in spite of the country's economic downturn. As of March 2010, 148,035 foreign workers were reported to be living in the city making up about 18 percent of the workforce, up from 131,132 in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Approximately one-fifth of all investment in the Czech Republic takes place in the city.</p>
<p>Almost one-half of the national income from tourism is spent in Prague. The city offers approximately 73,000 beds in accommodation facilities, most of which were built after 1990, including almost 51,000 beds in hotels and boarding houses.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Charles_Bridge_(Karl%C5%AFv_most),_Vltava_River,_Prague,_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Charles_Bridge_%28Karl%C5%AFv_most%29%2C_Vltava_River%2C_Prague%2C_2015.jpg/220px-Charles_Bridge_%28Karl%C5%AFv_most%29%2C_Vltava_River%2C_Prague%2C_2015.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Charles_Bridge_%28Karl%C5%AFv_most%29%2C_Vltava_River%2C_Prague%2C_2015.jpg/330px-Charles_Bridge_%28Karl%C5%AFv_most%29%2C_Vltava_River%2C_Prague%2C_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Charles_Bridge_%28Karl%C5%AFv_most%29%2C_Vltava_River%2C_Prague%2C_2015.jpg/440px-Charles_Bridge_%28Karl%C5%AFv_most%29%2C_Vltava_River%2C_Prague%2C_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="2238" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Charles_Bridge_(Karl%C5%AFv_most),_Vltava_River,_Prague,_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Charles Bridge (Karlův most), Vltava River, Prague, 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From the late 1990s to late 2000s, the city was a popular filming location for international productions such as Hollywood and Bollywood motion pictures. A combination of architecture, low costs and the existing motion picture infrastructure have proven attractive to international film production companies.</p>
<p>The modern economy of Prague is largely service and export-based and, in a 2010 survey, the city was named the best city in Central and Eastern Europe (CEE) for business.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, Prague was deemed among the three best cities in Central and Eastern Europe according to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a>'</i>s livability rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The city was named as a top-tier nexus city for innovation across multiple sectors of the global innovation economy, placing 29th globally out of 289 cities, ahead of <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a> for innovation in 2010 in 2thinknow annual analysts <a href="/w/index.php?title=Innovation_Cities_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Innovation Cities Index (page does not exist)">Innovation Cities Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-innovation_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-innovation-63">[63]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Na_p%C5%99%C3%ADkop%C4%9B" title="Na příkopě">Na příkopě</a> in New Town is the most expensive street in the whole of Central Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the Eurostat research, Prague ranked fifth among Europe's 271 regions in terms of gross domestic product per inhabitant, achieving 172 percent of the EU average. It ranked just above Paris and well above the country as a whole, which achieved 80 percent of the EU average.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>

<p>Since <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">the fall of the Iron Curtain</a>, Prague has become one of the world's most popular tourist destinations. Prague suffered considerably less damage during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> than some other major cities in the region, allowing most of its historic architecture to stay true to form. It contains one of the world's most pristine and varied collections of architecture, from <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_art" title="Romanesque art">Romanesque</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rococo" title="Rococo">Rococo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Revival_architecture" title="Renaissance Revival architecture">Neo-Renaissance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Neo-Gothic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cubism" title="Cubism">Cubist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neoclassicism" title="Neoclassicism">Neo-Classical</a> and ultra-modern.</p>
<p>Prague is classified as an "Alpha-" <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a> according to <a href="/wiki/GaWC" class="mw-redirect" title="GaWC">GaWC</a> studies, comparable to <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> Prague ranked sixth in the <a href="/wiki/Tripadvisor" class="mw-redirect" title="Tripadvisor">Tripadvisor</a> world list of best destinations in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-tripadvisor.com_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tripadvisor.com-12">[12]</a></sup> Its rich history makes it a popular tourist destination, and the city receives more than 6.4&#160;million international visitors annually, as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. Prague is the fifth most visited <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> city after <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bremner_2015_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bremner_2015-13">[13]</a></sup> Prague's low cost of living makes it a popular destination for expats relocating to Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Hradčany_and_Lesser_Town_(Malá_Strana)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hrad.C4.8Dany_and_Lesser_Town_.28Mal.C3.A1_Strana.29">Hradčany and Lesser Town (Malá Strana)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Hradčany and Lesser Town (Malá Strana)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prague_Castle" title="Prague Castle">Prague Castle</a> with the <a href="/wiki/St._Vitus_Cathedral" title="St. Vitus Cathedral">St. Vitus Cathedral</a> which stores the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Crown_Jewels" class="mw-redirect" title="Czech Crown Jewels">Czech Crown Jewels</a></li>
<li>The picturesque <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bridge" title="Charles Bridge">Charles Bridge</a> (Karlův most)</li>
<li>The Baroque <a href="/wiki/St._Nicholas_Church_(Lesser_Town)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Nicholas Church (Lesser Town)">Saint Nicholas Church</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Church_of_Our_Lady_Victorious" title="Church of Our Lady Victorious">Church of Our Lady Victorious</a> and <a href="/wiki/Infant_Jesus_of_Prague" title="Infant Jesus of Prague">Infant Jesus of Prague</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/P%C3%ADsek_Gate" title="Písek Gate">Písek Gate</a>, one of the last preserved city gate of Baroque fortification</li>
<li>Petřín Hill with <a href="/wiki/Pet%C5%99%C3%ADn_Lookout_Tower" title="Petřín Lookout Tower">Petřín Lookout Tower</a>, Mirror Maze and <a href="/wiki/Pet%C5%99%C3%ADn_funicular" title="Petřín funicular">Petřín funicular</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lennon_Wall" title="Lennon Wall">Lennon Wall</a></li>
<li>The Franz Kafka Museum</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kampa_Island" title="Kampa Island">Kampa Island</a>, an island with a view of the Charles Bridge<sup id="cite_ref-YourCzechRepublic.cz_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YourCzechRepublic.cz-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</div>
<h3><span id="Old_Town_(Staré_Město)_and_Josefov"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_Town_.28Star.C3.A9_M.C4.9Bsto.29_and_Josefov">Old Town (Staré Město) and Josefov</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Old Town (Staré Město) and Josefov">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Prague_Astronomical_Clock" class="mw-redirect" title="Prague Astronomical Clock">Astronomical Clock</a> (Orloj) on <a href="/wiki/Old_Town_(Prague)" title="Old Town (Prague)">Old Town</a> City Hall</li>
<li>The Gothic <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Our_Lady_before_T%C3%BDn" title="Church of Our Lady before Týn">Church of Our Lady before Týn</a> (Kostel Matky Boží před Týnem) from the 14th century with 80 m high towers</li>
<li>The vaulted Gothic <a href="/wiki/Old_New_Synagogue" title="Old New Synagogue">Old New Synagogue</a> (Staronová Synagoga) of 1270</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Old_Jewish_Cemetery,_Prague" title="Old Jewish Cemetery, Prague">Old Jewish Cemetery</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Powder_Tower" title="Powder Tower">Powder Tower</a> (Prašná brána), a Gothic tower of the old city gates</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Spanish_Synagogue_(Prague)" title="Spanish Synagogue (Prague)">Spanish Synagogue</a> with its beautiful interior</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Old_Town_Square_(Prague)" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Town Square (Prague)">Old Town Square</a> (Staroměstské náměstí) with gothic and baroque architectural styles</li>
<li>The art nouveau <a href="/wiki/Municipal_House" title="Municipal House">Municipal House</a>, a major civic landmark and concert hall known for its <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a> architectural style and political history in the Czech Republic.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Decorative_Arts_in_Prague" title="Museum of Decorative Arts in Prague">Museum of Decorative Arts in Prague</a>, with an extensive collections including glass, furniture, textile, toys, Art Nouveau, Cubism and Art Deco</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clam-Gallas_Palace" title="Clam-Gallas Palace">Clam-Gallas Palace</a>, a baroque palace from 1713</li>
</ul>
</div>
<h3><span id="New_Town_(Nové_Město)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Town_.28Nov.C3.A9_M.C4.9Bsto.29">New Town (Nové Město)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: New Town (Nové Město)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul>
<li>Busy and historic <a href="/wiki/Wenceslas_Square" title="Wenceslas Square">Wenceslas Square</a></li>
<li>The neo-renaissance <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_(Prague)" title="National Museum (Prague)">National Museum</a> with large scientific and historical collections</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre_(Prague)" title="National Theatre (Prague)">National Theatre</a>, a neo-Renaissance building with golden roof, alongside the banks of the Vltava river</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Deconstructivism" title="Deconstructivism">deconstructivist</a> <a href="/wiki/Dancing_House" title="Dancing House">Dancing House</a> (Fred and Ginger Building)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Square" title="Charles Square">Charles Square</a>, the largest medieval square in Europe (now turned into a park)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Emmaus_monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Emmaus monastery">Emmaus monastery</a> and WW Memorial "Prague to Its Victorious Sons" at Palacky Square (Palackého náměstí)</li>
<li>The museum of the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Anthropoid" title="Operation Anthropoid">Heydrich assassination</a> in the crypt of the <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Cathedral_of_Saints_Cyril_and_Methodius" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Cathedral of Saints Cyril and Methodius">Church of Saints Cyril and Methodius</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Stiassny" title="Wilhelm Stiassny">Stiassny</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_Synagogue" title="Jubilee Synagogue">Jubilee Synagogue</a> is the largest in Prague</li>
<li>The Mucha Museum, showcasing the <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a> works of <a href="/wiki/Alphonse_Mucha" title="Alphonse Mucha">Alphonse Mucha</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._Apollinaire,_Prague" title="Church of St. Apollinaire, Prague">Church of St. Apollinaire, Prague</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Church_of_Saint_Michael_the_Archangel_in_Prague" title="Church of Saint Michael the Archangel in Prague">Church of Saint Michael the Archangel in Prague</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<h3><span id="Vinohrady_and_Žižkov"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Vinohrady_and_.C5.BDi.C5.BEkov">Vinohrady and Žižkov</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Vinohrady and Žižkov">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_Monument_in_Vitkov" title="National Monument in Vitkov">National Monument in Vitkov</a> with a large bronze equestrian statue of <a href="/wiki/Jan_%C5%BDi%C5%BEka" title="Jan Žižka">Jan Žižka</a> in Vítkov Park, Žižkov&#160;– <a href="/wiki/Prague_3" title="Prague 3">Prague 3</a></li>
<li>The neo-Gothic <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._Ludmila" title="Church of St. Ludmila">Church of St. Ludmila</a> at <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A1m%C4%9Bst%C3%AD_M%C3%ADru" class="mw-redirect" title="Náměstí Míru">Náměstí Míru</a> (Peace Square) in <a href="/wiki/Vinohrady" title="Vinohrady">Vinohrady</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/%C5%BDi%C5%BEkov_Television_Tower" title="Žižkov Television Tower">Žižkov Television Tower</a> with sculptures of crawling babies</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_Jewish_Cemetery,_Prague" title="New Jewish Cemetery, Prague">New Jewish Cemetery</a> in Olšany, location of <a href="/wiki/Franz_Kafka" title="Franz Kafka">Franz Kafka</a>'s grave&#160;– <a href="/wiki/Prague_3" title="Prague 3">Prague 3</a></li>
<li>The Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/Sacred_Heart_Church_(Prague)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sacred Heart Church (Prague)">Sacred Heart Church</a> at <a href="/wiki/Ji%C5%99%C3%ADho_z_Pod%C4%9Bbrad" class="mw-redirect" title="Jiřího z Poděbrad">George of Poděbrady Square</a> (Jiřího z Poděbrad)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Vinohrady" title="Vinohrady">Vinohrady</a> grand Neo-Renaissance, Art Nouveau, Pseudo Baroque, and Neo-Gothic buildings in the area between <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A1m%C4%9Bst%C3%AD_M%C3%ADru" class="mw-redirect" title="Náměstí Míru">Náměstí Míru</a> (Peace Square), Jiřího z Poděbrad square and Havlíčkovy sady park<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_places">Other places</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Other places">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vy%C5%A1ehrad" title="Vyšehrad">Vyšehrad Castle</a> with <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_St_Peter_and_St_Paul" class="mw-redirect" title="Basilica of St Peter and St Paul">Basilica of St Peter and St Paul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vy%C5%A1ehrad_cemetery" title="Vyšehrad cemetery">Vyšehrad cemetery</a> and Prague oldest Rotunda of St. Martin</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Prague_Metronome" title="Prague Metronome">Prague Metronome</a> at <a href="/wiki/Letn%C3%A1_Park" title="Letná Park">Letná Park</a>, a giant, functional metronome that looms over the city</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prague_Zoo" title="Prague Zoo">Prague Zoo</a> in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Troja_(Prague)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Troja (Prague) (page does not exist)">Troja</a>, selected as one of the world's best zoos by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine<sup id="cite_ref-forbes-zoo_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-zoo-56">[56]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/V%C3%BDstavi%C5%A1t%C4%9B_Praha#Industrial_Palace" title="Výstaviště Praha">Industrial Palace</a> (Průmyslový palác), <a href="/wiki/V%C3%BDstavi%C5%A1t%C4%9B_Praha#K.C5.99i.C5.BE.C3.ADk.27s_light_fountain" title="Výstaviště Praha">Křižík's Light fountain</a>, funfair <a href="/wiki/Lunapark,_Prague" class="mw-redirect" title="Lunapark, Prague">Lunapark</a> and Sea World Aquarium in <a href="/wiki/V%C3%BDstavi%C5%A1t%C4%9B" class="mw-redirect" title="Výstaviště">Výstaviště compound</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hole%C5%A1ovice" title="Holešovice">Holešovice</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Letohr%C3%A1dek_Hv%C4%9Bzda" title="Letohrádek Hvězda">Letohrádek Hvězda</a> (Star Villa) in <a href="/wiki/Liboc" title="Liboc">Liboc</a>, a renaissance villa in the shape of a six-pointed star surrounded by a game reserve</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_Gallery_in_Prague" title="National Gallery in Prague">National Gallery in Prague</a> with large collection of Czech and international paintings and sculptures by artists such as <a href="/wiki/Alphonse_Mucha" title="Alphonse Mucha">Mucha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franti%C5%A1ek_Kupka" title="František Kupka">Kupka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Picasso" class="mw-redirect" title="Picasso">Picasso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monet" class="mw-redirect" title="Monet">Monet</a> or <a href="/wiki/Van_Gogh" class="mw-redirect" title="Van Gogh">Van Gogh</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/And%C4%9Bl_(neighborhood)" title="Anděl (neighborhood)">Anděl</a>, a busy part of the city with modern architecture and a shopping mall</li>
<li>The large <a href="/wiki/Nusle_Bridge" title="Nusle Bridge">Nusle Bridge</a>, spans the <a href="/wiki/Nusle" title="Nusle">Nusle</a> Valley, linking New Town to <a href="/wiki/Pankr%C3%A1c" title="Pankrác">Pankrác</a>, with the Metro running underneath the road</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Strahov_Monastery" title="Strahov Monastery">Strahov Monastery</a>, an old Czech <a href="/wiki/Premonstratensian" class="mw-redirect" title="Premonstratensian">premonstratensian</a> abbey founded in 1149 and monastic library</li>
</ul>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote selfreference">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Education_in_Prague" title="Category:Education in Prague">Category:Education in Prague</a>.</div>
<p>Twelve universities, and a number of colleges and schools are located in the city, including:</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_universities">Public universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Public universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span id="Science,_research_and_hi-tech_centres"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Science.2C_research_and_hi-tech_centres">Science, research and hi-tech centres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Science, research and hi-tech centres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote selfreference">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Science_and_technology_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Category:Science and technology in the Czech Republic">Category:Science and technology in the Czech Republic</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:N%C3%A1b%C5%99e%C5%BE%C3%AD_Kapit%C3%A1na_Jaro%C5%A1e,_budova_Galileo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/N%C3%A1b%C5%99e%C5%BE%C3%AD_Kapit%C3%A1na_Jaro%C5%A1e%2C_budova_Galileo.jpg/220px-N%C3%A1b%C5%99e%C5%BE%C3%AD_Kapit%C3%A1na_Jaro%C5%A1e%2C_budova_Galileo.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/N%C3%A1b%C5%99e%C5%BE%C3%AD_Kapit%C3%A1na_Jaro%C5%A1e%2C_budova_Galileo.jpg/330px-N%C3%A1b%C5%99e%C5%BE%C3%AD_Kapit%C3%A1na_Jaro%C5%A1e%2C_budova_Galileo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/N%C3%A1b%C5%99e%C5%BE%C3%AD_Kapit%C3%A1na_Jaro%C5%A1e%2C_budova_Galileo.jpg/440px-N%C3%A1b%C5%99e%C5%BE%C3%AD_Kapit%C3%A1na_Jaro%C5%A1e%2C_budova_Galileo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4898" data-file-height="3478" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:N%C3%A1b%C5%99e%C5%BE%C3%AD_Kapit%C3%A1na_Jaro%C5%A1e,_budova_Galileo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Galileo_(satellite_navigation)" title="Galileo (satellite navigation)">Galileo</a> system in Prague's <a href="/wiki/Hole%C5%A1ovice" title="Holešovice">Holešovice</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The region city of Prague is an important centre of research. It is the seat of 39 out of 54 institutes of the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Sciences_of_the_Czech_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy of Sciences of the Czech Republic">Czech Academy of Sciences</a>, including the largest ones, the Institute of Physics, the Institute of Microbiology and the Institute of Organic Chemistry and Biochemistry. It is also a seat of 10 public research institutes, four <a href="/wiki/Business_incubator" title="Business incubator">business incubators</a> and large hospitals performing <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> activities such as the Institute for Clinical and Experimental Medicine in Prague or the Motol University Hospital. Universities seated in Prague (see section <i>Colleges and Universities</i>) also represent important centres of science and research activities.</p>
<p>As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 13,000 researchers (out of 30,000 in the Czech Republic, counted in full-time equivalent), representing 3% share of Prague's economically active population. Gross expenditure on research and development accounted for €901.3&#160;million (41.5% of country's total).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some well-known multinational companies have established research and development facilities in Prague, among them <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a>.</p>
<p>Prague was selected to host administration of the EU satellite navigation system <a href="/wiki/Galileo_(satellite_navigation)" title="Galileo (satellite navigation)">Galileo</a>. It started to provide its first services in December 2016 and full completion is expected by 2020.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transportation">Public transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Public transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_07-2016_tram_at_Florenc.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Prague_07-2016_tram_at_Florenc.jpg/220px-Prague_07-2016_tram_at_Florenc.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Prague_07-2016_tram_at_Florenc.jpg/330px-Prague_07-2016_tram_at_Florenc.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Prague_07-2016_tram_at_Florenc.jpg/440px-Prague_07-2016_tram_at_Florenc.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4923" data-file-height="3282" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_07-2016_tram_at_Florenc.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/%C5%A0koda_15_T" title="Škoda 15 T">Škoda 15 T</a>, tram of the <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Prague" title="Trams in Prague">Prague tram system</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The public transport infrastructure (PID, <i>Pražská integrovaná doprava</i>) consists of a heavily used <a href="/wiki/Prague_Integrated_Transport" title="Prague Integrated Transport">integrated transport system</a> of <a href="/wiki/Prague_Metro" title="Prague Metro">Prague Metro</a> (lines <a href="/wiki/Line_A_(Prague_Metro)" title="Line A (Prague Metro)">A</a>, <a href="/wiki/Line_B_(Prague_Metro)" title="Line B (Prague Metro)">B</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Line_C_(Prague_Metro)" title="Line C (Prague Metro)">C</a> – its length is 65&#160;km (40&#160;mi) with 61 stations in total), <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Prague" title="Trams in Prague">Prague tram system</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buses_in_Prague" title="Buses in Prague">Prague buses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esko_Prague" title="Esko Prague">commuter S-trains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Funicular" title="Funicular">funiculars</a>, and six <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferries</a>. Prague has one of the highest rates of public transport usage in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> with 1.2 billion passenger journeys per year. Prague has about 130 bus lines (numbers 100–299) and 22 tram lines (numbers 1–26). There are also three funiculars, one on <a href="/wiki/Pet%C5%99%C3%ADn_Hill" class="mw-redirect" title="Petřín Hill">Petřín Hill</a>, one on Mrázovka Hill and a third at the <a href="/wiki/Prague_Zoo" title="Prague Zoo">Zoo in Troja</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_-_bus_112.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Prague_-_bus_112.jpg/220px-Prague_-_bus_112.jpg" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Prague_-_bus_112.jpg/330px-Prague_-_bus_112.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Prague_-_bus_112.jpg/440px-Prague_-_bus_112.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3728" data-file-height="2128" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prague_-_bus_112.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/SOR_NB_18" title="SOR NB 18">SOR NB 18</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Buses_in_Prague" title="Buses in Prague">Prague bus service</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Prague" title="Trams in Prague">The Prague tram system</a> now operates various types of trams: still popular classic <a href="/wiki/Tatra_T3" title="Tatra T3">Tatra T3</a>, newer <a href="/wiki/Tatra_KT8D5" title="Tatra KT8D5">Tatra KT8D5</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tatra_T6A5" title="Tatra T6A5">T6A5</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0koda_14_T" title="Škoda 14 T">Škoda 14 T</a> (designed by <a href="/wiki/Porsche_Design_Group" title="Porsche Design Group">Porsche</a>), newest modern <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0koda_15_T" title="Škoda 15 T">Škoda 15 T</a> and nostalgic tram lines 23 and 41. Although Melbourne, Australia has the longest total tram system length in the world, Prague's tram network is one of the largest in the world by other measures.</p>
<p>The Prague tram rolling stock consists of over 900 individual cars, of those around 400 are the modernized <a href="/wiki/Tatra_T3" title="Tatra T3">T3</a> class, which are typically operated coupled together in pairs. The system carries more than 356 million passengers annually, the highest tram patronage in the world after <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>. On a per capita basis, Prague has the second highest tram patronage after <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a>.</p>
<p>All services have a common ticketing system, and are run by the Prague Public Transport Company (Dopravní podnik hl. m. Prahy, a. s.) and several other companies. Recently, the <i>Regional Organiser of Prague Integrated Transport (ROPID)</i> has franchised operation of ferries on the <a href="/wiki/Vltava" title="Vltava">Vltava</a> river, which are also a part of the public transport system with common fares. <a href="/wiki/Taxicab" title="Taxicab">Taxi</a> services make pick-ups on the streets or operate from regulated taxi stands.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Prague_Metro">Prague Metro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Prague Metro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">Metro</a> has three major lines extending throughout the city: A (green), B (yellow) and C (red). A fourth Metro line is planned, which would connect the city centre to southern parts of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The Prague Metro system served 589.2 million passengers in 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-annual-report-2012_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annual-report-2012-75">[75]</a></sup> making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_metro_systems" title="List of metro systems">fifth busiest metro system in Europe</a> and the most-patronised in the world on a per capita basis. The first section of the Prague metro was put into operation in 1974. It was the stretch between stations <a href="/wiki/Ka%C4%8Derov" class="mw-redirect" title="Kačerov">Kačerov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Florenc_(Prague_Metro)" title="Florenc (Prague Metro)">Florenc</a> on the current <a href="/wiki/Line_C_(Prague_Metro)" title="Line C (Prague Metro)">line C</a>. The first part of <a href="/wiki/Line_A_(Prague_Metro)" title="Line A (Prague Metro)">Line A</a> was opened in 1978 (<a href="/wiki/Dejvick%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Dejvická">Dejvická</a> – <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A1m%C4%9Bst%C3%AD_M%C3%ADru" class="mw-redirect" title="Náměstí Míru">Náměstí Míru</a>), the first part of <a href="/wiki/Line_B_(Prague_Metro)" title="Line B (Prague Metro)">line B</a> in 1985 (<a href="/wiki/And%C4%9Bl_(Prague_Metro)" title="Anděl (Prague Metro)">Anděl</a> – <a href="/wiki/Florenc_(Prague_Metro)" title="Florenc (Prague Metro)">Florenc</a>).</p>
<p>In April 2015, construction finished to extend the green line A further into the northwest corner of Prague closer to the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> A new interchange station for the bus in the direction of the airport is now the station <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD_Veleslav%C3%ADn_(Prague_Metro)" title="Nádraží Veleslavín (Prague Metro)">Nádraží Veleslavín</a>. The final station of the green line is <a href="/wiki/Nemocnice_Motol" title="Nemocnice Motol">Nemocnice Motol</a> (Motol Hospital), giving people direct public transportation access to the largest medical facility in the Czech Republic and one of the largest in Europe. A railway connection to the airport is planned.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Praha,_N%C3%A1rodn%C3%AD_t%C5%99%C3%ADda,_Odj%C3%AD%C5%BEd%C4%9Bj%C3%ADc%C3%AD_vlak.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Praha%2C_N%C3%A1rodn%C3%AD_t%C5%99%C3%ADda%2C_Odj%C3%AD%C5%BEd%C4%9Bj%C3%ADc%C3%AD_vlak.jpg/220px-Praha%2C_N%C3%A1rodn%C3%AD_t%C5%99%C3%ADda%2C_Odj%C3%AD%C5%BEd%C4%9Bj%C3%ADc%C3%AD_vlak.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Praha%2C_N%C3%A1rodn%C3%AD_t%C5%99%C3%ADda%2C_Odj%C3%AD%C5%BEd%C4%9Bj%C3%ADc%C3%AD_vlak.jpg/330px-Praha%2C_N%C3%A1rodn%C3%AD_t%C5%99%C3%ADda%2C_Odj%C3%AD%C5%BEd%C4%9Bj%C3%ADc%C3%AD_vlak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Praha%2C_N%C3%A1rodn%C3%AD_t%C5%99%C3%ADda%2C_Odj%C3%AD%C5%BEd%C4%9Bj%C3%ADc%C3%AD_vlak.jpg/440px-Praha%2C_N%C3%A1rodn%C3%AD_t%C5%99%C3%ADda%2C_Odj%C3%AD%C5%BEd%C4%9Bj%C3%ADc%C3%AD_vlak.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2160" data-file-height="1440" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Praha,_N%C3%A1rodn%C3%AD_t%C5%99%C3%ADda,_Odj%C3%AD%C5%BEd%C4%9Bj%C3%ADc%C3%AD_vlak.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Prague_Metro" title="Prague Metro">Prague Metro</a> station <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A1rodn%C3%AD_t%C5%99%C3%ADda_(Prague_Metro)" title="Národní třída (Prague Metro)">Národní třída</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In operation there are currently two kinds of units: "<a href="/w/index.php?title=81-71M&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="81-71M (page does not exist)">81-71M</a>" which is modernized variant of the Soviet <a href="/wiki/81-717/714" class="mw-redirect" title="81-717/714">81-71</a> (completely modernized between 1995 and 2003) and new "<a href="/wiki/Metro_M1_(Prague)" title="Metro M1 (Prague)">Metro M1</a>" trains (since 2000), manufactured by consortium consisting of <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C4%8CKD_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="ČKD (company)">ČKD Praha</a> and <a href="/wiki/ADtranz" class="mw-redirect" title="ADtranz">ADtranz</a>. The minimum interval between two trains is 90 seconds.</p>
<p>The original Soviet vehicles "<a href="/wiki/Metrovagonmash_E%C4%8Ds" title="Metrovagonmash Ečs">Ečs</a>" were excluded in 1997, but one vehicle is placed in public transport museum in depot <a href="/wiki/St%C5%99e%C5%A1ovice" title="Střešovice">Střešovice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A1m%C4%9Bst%C3%AD_M%C3%ADru" class="mw-redirect" title="Náměstí Míru">Náměstí Míru</a> metro station is the deepest station and is equipped with the longest <a href="/wiki/Escalator" title="Escalator">escalator</a> in <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Prague_metro" class="mw-redirect" title="Prague metro">Prague metro</a> is generally considered very safe.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barrande_bridge.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Barrande_bridge.JPG/220px-Barrande_bridge.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Barrande_bridge.JPG/330px-Barrande_bridge.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Barrande_bridge.JPG/440px-Barrande_bridge.JPG 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="720" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barrande_bridge.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Barrandov bridge, part of the City (inner) Ring Road</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The main flow of traffic leads through the centre of the city and through inner and outer ring roads (partially in operation).</p>
<p><b>Inner Ring Road (The City Ring "MO"):</b> Once completed it will surround the wider central part of the city. The longest city <a href="/wiki/Tunnel" title="Tunnel">tunnel</a> in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> with a length of 5.5 kilometres (3.4 miles) and five interchanges has been completed to relieve congestion in the north-western part of Prague. Called <i><b><a href="/wiki/Blanka_tunnel_complex" title="Blanka tunnel complex">Blanka tunnel complex</a></b></i> and part of the City Ring Road, it was estimated to eventually cost&#160;– after several increases&#160;– 43&#160;billion <a href="/wiki/Czech_koruna" title="Czech koruna">CZK</a>. Construction started in 2007 and, after repeated delays, the tunnel was officially opened in September 2015. This tunnel complex completes a major part of the inner ring road. It is expected that the whole city ring will not be completed before 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p><b><a href="/w/index.php?title=D0_expressway_(Czech_Republic)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="D0 expressway (Czech Republic) (page does not exist)">Outer Ring Road</a> (The Prague Ring "D0"):</b> This ring road will connect all major motorways and speedways that meet each other in Prague region and provide faster transit without a necessity to drive through the city. So far 39&#160;km (24&#160;mi), out of a total planned 83&#160;km (52&#160;mi), is in operation. The year of full completion is unknown due to incompetent, constantly changing, leadership of Czech Road and Motorway Directorate, lack of administrative preparations, and insufficient funding of road constructions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Most recently, the southern part of this road (with a length of more than 20&#160;km (12&#160;mi)) was opened on 22 September 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Praha_hlavn%C3%AD_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD_(celkov%C3%BD_pohled).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Praha_hlavn%C3%AD_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD_%28celkov%C3%BD_pohled%29.jpg/220px-Praha_hlavn%C3%AD_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD_%28celkov%C3%BD_pohled%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Praha_hlavn%C3%AD_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD_%28celkov%C3%BD_pohled%29.jpg/330px-Praha_hlavn%C3%AD_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD_%28celkov%C3%BD_pohled%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Praha_hlavn%C3%AD_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD_%28celkov%C3%BD_pohled%29.jpg/440px-Praha_hlavn%C3%AD_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD_%28celkov%C3%BD_pohled%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3713" data-file-height="2475" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Praha_hlavn%C3%AD_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD_(celkov%C3%BD_pohled).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Praha_hlavn%C3%AD_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD" title="Praha hlavní nádraží">Prague main railway station</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city forms the hub of the <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cesk%C3%A9_dr%C3%A1hy" title="České dráhy">Czech railway</a> system, with services to all parts of the country and abroad. The railway system links Prague with major European cities (which can be reached without transfers), including <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a> (Germany); <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> (Austria); <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cracow" class="mw-redirect" title="Cracow">Cracow</a> (Poland); <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice" title="Košice">Košice</a> (Slovakia); <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a> (Hungary); <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a> (Switzerland); <a href="/wiki/Split,_Croatia" title="Split, Croatia">Split</a> (Croatia); <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> (Serbia) and <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> (Russia). Travel times range between 4.5 hours to Berlin and 27 hours to Moscow.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prague's main international railway station is <a href="/wiki/Praha_hlavn%C3%AD_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD" title="Praha hlavní nádraží">Hlavní nádraží</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> rail services are also available from other main stations: <a href="/wiki/Praha_Masarykovo_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD" title="Praha Masarykovo nádraží">Masarykovo nádraží</a>, <a href="/wiki/Praha-Hole%C5%A1ovice_railway_station" title="Praha-Holešovice railway station">Holešovice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Praha-Sm%C3%ADchov_railway_station" title="Praha-Smíchov railway station">Smíchov</a>, in addition to suburban stations. Commuter rail services operate under the name <a href="/wiki/Esko_Prague" title="Esko Prague">Esko Praha</a>, which is part of <a href="/wiki/Prague_Integrated_Transport" title="Prague Integrated Transport">PID</a> (Prague Integrated Transport]].</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_to_Prague_airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Entrance_to_Prague_airport.jpg/220px-Entrance_to_Prague_airport.jpg" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Entrance_to_Prague_airport.jpg/330px-Entrance_to_Prague_airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Entrance_to_Prague_airport.jpg/440px-Entrance_to_Prague_airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3112" data-file-height="2113" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_to_Prague_airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport_Prague" title="Václav Havel Airport Prague">Václav Havel Airport Prague</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Prague is served by <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Havel_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Václav Havel Airport">Václav Havel Airport</a>, the largest airport in the Czech Republic and one of the largest airports in central and eastern <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. The airport was named after the first Czech President, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-19854293">Vaclav Havel</a>. Vaclav Havel was also the ninth and last president of Czechoslovakia. The airport is the hub of the flag carrier, <a href="/wiki/Czech_Airlines" title="Czech Airlines">Czech Airlines</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> as well as of the low-cost airlines <a href="/wiki/SmartWings" title="SmartWings">SmartWings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a> operating throughout Europe. Other airports in Prague include the city's original airport in the north-eastern district of <a href="/wiki/Kbely" class="mw-redirect" title="Kbely">Kbely</a>, which is serviced by the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Air_Force" title="Czech Air Force">Czech Air Force</a>, also internationally. The runway (9–27) at Kbely is 2&#160;km (1&#160;mi) long. The airport also houses the <a href="/wiki/Prague_Aviation_Museum,_Kbely" class="mw-redirect" title="Prague Aviation Museum, Kbely">Prague Aviation Museum</a>. The nearby <a href="/wiki/Let%C5%88any" title="Letňany">Letňany</a> airport is mainly used for private aviation and aeroclub aviation. Another airport in the proximity is <a href="/wiki/Aero_Vodochody" title="Aero Vodochody">Aero Vodochody</a> aircraft factory to the north, used for testing purposes, as well as for aeroclub aviation. There are a few aeroclubs around Prague, such as the <a href="https://cs.wikipedia.org/wiki/To%C4%8Dn%C3%A1" class="extiw" title="cs:Točná">Točná</a> airfield.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Prague" title="Football in Prague">Football in Prague</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:O2_Arena,_od_%C4%8Ceskomoravsk%C3%A9.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/O2_Arena%2C_od_%C4%8Ceskomoravsk%C3%A9.jpg/220px-O2_Arena%2C_od_%C4%8Ceskomoravsk%C3%A9.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/O2_Arena%2C_od_%C4%8Ceskomoravsk%C3%A9.jpg/330px-O2_Arena%2C_od_%C4%8Ceskomoravsk%C3%A9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/O2_Arena%2C_od_%C4%8Ceskomoravsk%C3%A9.jpg/440px-O2_Arena%2C_od_%C4%8Ceskomoravsk%C3%A9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:O2_Arena,_od_%C4%8Ceskomoravsk%C3%A9.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/O2_Arena_(Prague)" title="O2 Arena (Prague)">O2 Arena</a> was built to host the <a href="/wiki/2004_Men%27s_World_Ice_Hockey_Championships" title="2004 Men's World Ice Hockey Championships">2004 Men's World Ice Hockey Championships</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Prague is the site of many sports events, national stadiums and teams.</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">

<li>World <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_(sport)" title="Ultimate (sport)">Ultimate</a> Club Championships 2010<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PetrinObservationTower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/PetrinObservationTower.jpg/170px-PetrinObservationTower.jpg" width="170" height="262" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/PetrinObservationTower.jpg/255px-PetrinObservationTower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/PetrinObservationTower.jpg/340px-PetrinObservationTower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1040" data-file-height="1600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PetrinObservationTower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Pet%C5%99%C3%ADn_Lookout_Tower" title="Petřín Lookout Tower">Petřín Lookout Tower</a>, an observation tower built at Petřín hill.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city of Prague maintains its own EU delegation in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> called Prague House.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prague was the location of <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">U.S. President</a> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>'s speech on 5 April 2009, which led to the <a href="/wiki/New_START" title="New START">New START</a> treaty with Russia, signed in Prague on 8 April 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>The annual conference <a href="/wiki/Forum_2000" title="Forum 2000">Forum 2000</a>, which was founded by former Czech President <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Havel" title="Václav Havel">Václav Havel</a>, Japanese philanthropist <a href="/wiki/Y%C5%8Dhei_Sasakawa" title="Yōhei Sasakawa">Yōhei Sasakawa</a>, and Nobel Peace Prize laureate <a href="/wiki/Elie_Wiesel" title="Elie Wiesel">Elie Wiesel</a> in 1996, is held in Prague. Its main objective is "to identify the key issues facing civilization and to explore ways to prevent the escalation of conflicts that have religion, culture or ethnicity as their primary components", and also intends to promote democracy in non-democratic countries and to support civil society. Conferences have attracted a number of prominent thinkers, Nobel laureates, former and acting politicians, business leaders and other individuals like: <a href="/wiki/F._W._de_Klerk" title="F. W. de Klerk">Frederik Willem de Klerk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Winton" title="Nicholas Winton">Nicholas Winton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Arias_S%C3%A1nchez" class="mw-redirect" title="Oscar Arias Sánchez">Oscar Arias Sánchez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dalai_Lama" title="Dalai Lama">Dalai Lama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hans_K%C3%BCng" title="Hans Küng">Hans Küng</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shimon_Peres" title="Shimon Peres">Shimon Peres</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madeleine_Albright" title="Madeleine Albright">Madeleine Albright</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Namesakes">Namesakes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Namesakes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A number of other settlements are derived or similar to the name of Prague. In many of these cases, Czech emigration has left a number of namesake cities scattered over the globe, with a notable concentration in the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>.</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr valign="top">
<td>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Praha,_Slovakia" title="Praha, Slovakia">Praha, Slovakia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Praha,_Texas" title="Praha, Texas">Praha, Texas</a>, United States<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prague,_Oklahoma" title="Prague, Oklahoma">Prague, Oklahoma</a>, United States<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prague,_Nebraska" title="Prague, Nebraska">Prague, Nebraska</a>, United States<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_Prague,_Minnesota" title="New Prague, Minnesota">New Prague, Minnesota</a>, United States<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Praga" title="Praga">Praga</a>, a historical borough of <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Capital_(political)" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital (political)">capital</a> of <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Additionally, <a href="/wiki/K%C5%82odzko" title="Kłodzko">Kłodzko</a> is traditionally referred to as "Little Prague" (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i>Klein-Prag</i></span>). Although now in <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, the city was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemian</a> <a href="/wiki/Kraj" title="Kraj">kraj</a> of the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Kladsko" title="County of Kladsko">County of Kladsko</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Prague&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">

April 1389<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">16 June</span> 2009</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APrague&amp;rft.btitle=The+former+Jewish+Quarter+in+Prague&amp;rft.date=1389&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.pub=prague.cz&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.prague.cz%2Fjewish-quarter%2F&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This swallow-tailed banner is approximately 4 by 6 feet (1.2 by 1.8 metres), with a red field sprinkled with small white fleurs-de-lis, and a silver old Town Coat-of-Arms in the centre. The words <i>PÁN BŮH POMOC NAŠE</i> (The Lord God is our Help) appeared above the coat-of-arms, with a Hussite "host with chalice" centred on the top. Near the swallow-tails is a crescent shaped golden sun with rays protruding. One of these banners was captured by Swedish troops in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Prague_(1648)" title="Battle of Prague (1648)">Battle of Prague (1648)</a>, when they captured the western bank of the Vltava river and were repulsed from the eastern bank, they placed it in the Royal Military Museum in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>; although this flag still exists, it is in very poor condition. They also took the <a href="/wiki/Codex_Gigas" title="Codex Gigas">Codex Gigas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Codex_Argenteus" title="Codex Argenteus">Codex Argenteus</a>. The earliest evidence indicates that a gonfalon with a municipal charge painted on it was used for Old Town as early as 1419. Since this city militia flag was in use before 1477 and during the Hussite Wars, it is the oldest still preserved municipal flag of Bohemia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></span></li>
